<span id="freeTextContainer2775517964362460351">I kinda neglected Colton and Driven series...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508745525ra/24249300.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*sigh*<br/><br/>I know...I mean, I don't know...why or how...but NOW that I've finished book 2 and almost instantly remembering the piled up angsty shit from book 1, it didn't take long for me to pick up on the burried angsty aggeavating notion spured in me by the content of this sequel...<br/><br/>So, the bottom line is, they are both broken, hurt, but Colton is more damaged emotionally and physically due to abuse from him childhood that had him growing up with a distor</span>
  <span id="freeText2775517964362460351" style="display:none">I kinda neglected Colton and Driven series...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508745525ra/24249300.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*sigh*<br><br>I know...I mean, I don't know...why or how...but NOW that I've finished book 2 and almost instantly remembering the piled up angsty shit from book 1, it didn't take long for me to pick up on the burried angsty aggeavating notion spured in me by the content of this sequel...<br><br>So, the bottom line is, they are both broken, hurt, but Colton is more damaged emotionally and physically due to abuse from him childhood that had him growing up with a distorted perception of love and what it means altogether...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>if you look past the gorgeously rough exterior…there’s a scared little boy inside that’s afraid of love. That for some reason he associates love with horrific expectations one minute and then thinks he’s not worthy of it the next. I think he’s afraid to love someone because he knows that they’ll leave. He’ll most likely hurt you to prove that you will...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But since the pull and chemistry Colton feels with Rylee makes him feel good and happy for the first time in a very long time considering...<br>And then she the infamous three little words that mean a helluwa lot slip from her lips : <i>I love you</i><br><br>And then all the pent up angst of stubborn chase/catch, push/pull between them starts that somehow escalates into a overbearing and irritating sequences wher you just want to fuckin slap the shit out of both of them and tell them to fuckin own their shit, "make it or break it" cause you are fuckin annoying...<br><br>Gah...<br><br>And then well, the cliffy ending slaps you back in the face...<br><br>Thank you very much!<br><br>And since I hate having loose ends, I need to read book 3 now, cause if i leave it hanging and out of my reading schedule God knows when I m gonna pick it up next... *sigh* LOL<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508745525ra/24249301.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_707527032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/707527032" />
    <a title="Pam Godwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10980625-pam-godwin"><img alt="Pam Godwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545404744p2/10980625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/707527032?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam Godwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam Godwin" href="/user/show/10980625-pam-godwin">Pam Godwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980625-pam-godwin?shelf=loaner">loaner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980625-pam-godwin?shelf=5-star-erotica">5-star-erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980625-pam-godwin?shelf=5-star-romance">5-star-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer707527032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17492404532098778948">Colton outshines in this second installment of the Driven Trilogy by making a tremendous effort in his turbulent relationship with Rylee. He is courageous in the shadows of his creeping memories. He becomes a hero worth rooting for.<br/><br/>Rylee, on the other hand, is the sum of everything I despise in a leading lady. She's unattractively catty, immature, passive-aggressive, whimper-y, and avoids communication in lieu of running off her mouth. She doesn't listen. She runs away. Always running. Always wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17492404532098778948" style="display:none">Colton outshines in this second installment of the Driven Trilogy by making a tremendous effort in his turbulent relationship with Rylee. He is courageous in the shadows of his creeping memories. He becomes a hero worth rooting for.<br /><br />Rylee, on the other hand, is the sum of everything I despise in a leading lady. She's unattractively catty, immature, passive-aggressive, whimper-y, and avoids communication in lieu of running off her mouth. She doesn't listen. She runs away. Always running. Always whimpering.<br /><br />The conflict is wholly based on a misunderstanding, made worse by Colton and Rylee's failure to discuss it. Would there have been a story if she'd just shut up and let him talk? No, but the constant relationship drama and the pages and pages of spiteful bickering keeps you engaged in a nerve-shredding, spit-flinging, positively frustrating way. Especially when you already know how things will end. You'll predict the cliffhanger chapters in advance. Everything about this story is predictable, because there's nothing unique here. <br /><br />But I loved it. When I was forced to put the book down, I did so relunctantly. Maybe it's the evocative way it's written. Maybe it's all the raw heat blazing between Colton and Rylee, and the hot, hot, scorching hot sex scenes. Maybe it's the merciless drive to screw with your emotions until you're ready to become a beserker right along with the characters. Whatever it is, it puts you through the wringer and turns you into a glutton for more messy emotional chaos.<br /><br />So, while this book is a compilation of all my peeves (cliffhanger, cliches, unlikeable heroine, contrived conflict), Colton and his drama penetrates and hooks. His aboutface will charm you, warm you, and make you care about what happens to him. I'd put up with the most unsavory of heroines just to spend more time with Ace.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17492404532098778948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21725822-hanne?shelf=coyer_summer2017">coyer_summer2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2079056568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4530326817744429562">Fueled picks up there where Driven ended. I loved this book even more than Driven. It was an emotional rollercoaster most of time, but it was also beautiful and romantic. Rylee and Colton grow closer and they fall in love. I got to know Rylee and Colton a little better and I love both of them even more.<br/><br/>My heart already broke for Colton in the first chapter. His past is horrible. It was a big mystery in the previous book, but I learnt about it in this book. I understand Colton’s decisions and act</span>
  <span id="freeText4530326817744429562" style="display:none">Fueled picks up there where Driven ended. I loved this book even more than Driven. It was an emotional rollercoaster most of time, but it was also beautiful and romantic. Rylee and Colton grow closer and they fall in love. I got to know Rylee and Colton a little better and I love both of them even more.<br /><br />My heart already broke for Colton in the first chapter. His past is horrible. It was a big mystery in the previous book, but I learnt about it in this book. I understand Colton’s decisions and actions better now. He’s damaged and he still fights against demons. Colton is a passionate and talented driver. Racing helps him and it’s everything to him, but he realizes that Rylee also helps him. She’s everything he never expected to have and someone who he needs.<br /><br />Rylee is the same woman as before, only a little stronger. She wants to be Colton and she’s falling hard for him. She will fight for him, give him place when he needs it and give him multiple chances. But she also has to protect her heart. <br /><br />There was some push and pull between Colton and Rylee. They want each other, but push the other away for their own reasons. When Colton is ready to have a real relationship with Rylee, he gives it his all. I loved reading about Colton’s change. Colton and Rylee are so good and so hot together. They are a beautiful couple.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4530326817744429562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_621600822" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621600822" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Liz)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5495317-elizabeth-liz"><img alt="Elizabeth (Liz)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551206872p2/5495317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621600822?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Liz)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Liz)" href="/user/show/5495317-elizabeth-liz">Elizabeth (Liz)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=ebook-read">ebook-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=erotica-romantica-read">erotica-romantica-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=contemporary-romance-read">contemporary-romance-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=arc-from-author-read">arc-from-author-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621600822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13606094249750997396"><blockquote>“Spiderman.  Batman.  Superman.  Ironman.”</blockquote><br/> <br/>Who knew that a random list of superheroes could literally produce chills throughout my entire body every time it appeared in Fueled, the second book in K. Bromberg’s amazing Driven Trilogy?!  Until you read the book, I realize you won’t have a clue what I’m talking about.  However, trust me when I tell you that this line is one of the single best in this book and probably in any book in recent memory!  It was used brilliantly, and, in those moments whe</span>
  <span id="freeText13606094249750997396" style="display:none"><blockquote>“Spiderman.  Batman.  Superman.  Ironman.”</blockquote><br /> <br />Who knew that a random list of superheroes could literally produce chills throughout my entire body every time it appeared in Fueled, the second book in K. Bromberg’s amazing Driven Trilogy?!  Until you read the book, I realize you won’t have a clue what I’m talking about.  However, trust me when I tell you that this line is one of the single best in this book and probably in any book in recent memory!  It was used brilliantly, and, in those moments when it appeared, it said everything without really needing to say anything—and it did so with rare perfection.  It evoked so much emotion in me…as a reader, a woman, and a human being.  There were multiple layers of meaning and importance in this one, seemingly inconsequential, thought, and I swear that I could see and feel each and every one of them when I read it.  This line, and one other, define who Colton Donovan was and is, at least at this point in time, and I believe that was the main goal and the greatest achievement of Fueled.  <br /> <br />In Driven, I came to know, connect with and care about Rylee.  I’m happy to say that she was still that same wonderful woman.  She’s so kind, unshakable, and driven (no pun intended) in her goals and love for the boys in her care, and in her determination to understand and help heal the man she loves.  Rylee did some growing, as well, in this second book.  I was thrilled to see her make strides in holding her ground against the force of nature that is Colton Donovan.  I jumped for joy when she demanded to be treated with respect, and, if that didn’t occur, then there would be nothing left between them!  I could feel that she was really making the attempt to demand her due from Colton, even as she was terrified that doing so might drive him away completely.  I came away from Fueled with even more admiration for Rylee than I had at the end of Driven!<br /> <br />I’m so, so pleased with the growth of Ryle and Colton as a couple in Fueled.  The relationship was deeper with a new, more serious layer of intensity.  I could truly feel them in this second book, both as individuals and as a couple.  I finally understood exactly what drew these two together in the first place and what continued to keep them both invested.  Rylee was drawn to the complexity of Colton’s combination of alpha male and truly vulnerable, deeply hurt man-boy.  Colton was drawn by Rylee’s genuine goodness, almost-innocence and her refusal to fall in line with his plans as every other woman in his life had.  They each drew certain lines in the sand, threw up obstacles and, oftentimes, reacted from a place of fear and pain.  However, with work and compromise, they eventually found ways to keep their relationship moving forward, struggle or not.  Colton and Rylee were particularly beautiful, real and amazing together in Fueled.  There’s not a doubt in my mind about these two.<br /> <br />By the way, the electricity and heat these two generated together could likely have powered a small city!  If what you’re really sitting there thinking is, “Just tell us how HOT this book is already!”, I can promise you will not be disappointed in any way.  Let’s just say Fueled revved my engine (pun intended) and kept it running at high speed for the length of this book!  Holy hotness, Batman!!  As usual, Haddie, Rylee’s best friend, puts it best.<br /> <br /> <br /><blockquote>“C’mon, spill the deets for dried up old me.  How’s his Aussie kiss?…”</blockquote><br /> <br /><blockquote>I blush a deep crimson, loving and hating her at the same time.  “Aussie kiss?  What in the hell are you talking about?”</blockquote><br /> <br /><blockquote>She lets out a naughty laugh and has an impish gleam in her eyes.  “How’s his mouth down under?”…</blockquote><br /> <br /><blockquote>I squeeze my eyes shut in embarrassment, unable to look at her.  “Well I’d say he speaks Australian like a damn native.”</blockquote><br /> <br /> <br /><blockquote>Haddie makes a soft noise in the back of her throat.  “Damn.  That face is a definite work of art.  You need to make sure you frame it between your legs every chance you get.”</blockquote><br /> <br /> <br />However, the real story of Fueled, was undoubtedly Colton Donovan.  I was gifted with far more than a small glimpse into what it is that makes Colton Donovan…well, Colton Donovan.  I can’t go into detail because I would never want to spoil the reading experience for you.  But I will say that after Driven, I was not 100% sure about Mr. Donovan.  He was most assuredly an alpha, and I saw flashes of what was underneath, but I needed this book, and I don’t even think I realized quite how true that was.  As I said earlier, I could feel Colton this time.  I got him, finally.  And, wow, what a story he has, which continues to unfold.  There were moments where I hurt for him so badly.  I came away from Fueled madly in love with Colton and squarely behind him in the inner battle that lies ahead.  I respected, admired and connected with him, and I couldn’t honestly say that after Driven.  Truly, Fueled gave me the gift of getting to know aspects of the real Colton Donovan for the first time, and I am incredibly grateful!<br /> <br />Fueled had a truly unforgettable ending!!  It was breathtaking, emotional, thrilling, frightening, amazing, beautiful, and crafted so f***ing well by K. Bromberg!  I honestly couldn’t turn the pages quickly enough.  It’s one of the best endings I’ve ever read, and that might surprise you once you’ve read the book!  In a series like this, readers have to be smart enough to know that Rylee and Colton’s story won’t be resolved in the second book.  For me, it’s part of what makes reading these series fun.  I know I’ll be getting more of the characters and story that I love.  It’s that simple.  So, enjoy the ending for what it is…and, most especially, where you know it will lead!<br /> <br />Here is where I have to give HUGE props—well-deserved, unquestionably-earned, HUGE props—to author K. Bromberg.  When I read and reviewed Driven months ago, I ultimately gave it four stars because it was a very enjoyable and entertaining story.  However, I was also completely honest in my review about those things which didn’t quite work for me.  I saw so much potential for where Rylee and Colton’s story could go, and I sensed that there was so much more to this author.  But nothing, I mean nothing, prepared me for the sheer growth, talent and natural ability of K. Bromberg’s writing in Fueled!  K. dug deep, deep down for this one, and it shows in every way, in all the best ways!  This story was flawlessly crafted, and I guarantee that Fueled easily sets the new bar for this genre!  <br /> <br />Don’t even question it.  If you’ve read Driven, you simply must read Fueled!  If you haven’t yet read Driven, do yourself a favor and go grab both of these books!  I simply can’t imagine not falling in love with these characters and their story!!<br /> <br /><blockquote>His smile lights up.  A solid figure standing still while everyone else moves in one big blur around him.  His eyes hold mine, intense and clear.  “I race you, Ryles,” he says in a voice that’s implacable and unwavering amidst the swirling chaos.<br /> <br />”I race you too, Colton.”  I mouth to him.  Despite the noise, I know he hears what I’ve said for a shy smile graces his lips, and he shakes his head like he’s trying to understand all of this too.<br /> <br />Love swells, overwhelms, and heals my heart that I once thought was irreparable.  Fills me with happiness over the man that I can’t tear my eyes away from.<br /> <br />My storm before the calm.<br /> <br />My angel breaking through the darkness.<br /> <br />My ace.</blockquote><br /> <br /> <br />5+++++ Stars!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>For more reviews, please visit <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Reviews</a> or visit us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></b>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13606094249750997396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/699481860?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog">Gitte TotallyBookedBlog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer699481860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13336333852252397287">Jointly Reviewed on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/08/26/fueled-the-driven-trilogy-2-by-k-bromberg-review-giveaway/'>http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/08/...</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380421924i/838831._SX540_.png' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>Jenny:</b> Well, we were left hanging at the end of Driven Book #1 in the Driven Trilogy and to be honest we were a little nervous about what to expect in this second installment weren’t we G? Our concerns were that, being a trilogy, this book could possibly fall in the dreaded “filler” trap, as is the case with some trilogies.<br/><br/>How wrong we were! Fueled is anything but a filler! Fueled is an essential component of this story and it almost </span>
  <span id="freeText13336333852252397287" style="display:none">Jointly Reviewed on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/08/26/fueled-the-driven-trilogy-2-by-k-bromberg-review-giveaway/">http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/08/...</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380421924i/838831._SX540_.png" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Jenny:</b> Well, we were left hanging at the end of Driven Book #1 in the Driven Trilogy and to be honest we were a little nervous about what to expect in this second installment weren’t we G? Our concerns were that, being a trilogy, this book could possibly fall in the dreaded “filler” trap, as is the case with some trilogies.<br><br>How wrong we were! Fueled is anything but a filler! Fueled is an essential component of this story and it almost felt as if Driven was a stepping stone leading us to Fueled. Oh the heat factor is still off the charts and the chemistry between Rylee and Colton is in stratospheric proportions, but this book had so much more, it had substance, secrets were uncovered, it was extremely intense at times, very emotional and an absolute must read! I have to say bravo to K Bromberg because she really took this one to a new level in the trilogy stakes that’s for sure! Fans and new readers alike devour this one, don’t you think so Gitte?<br><br><b>Gitte:</b> Hell yes Jenny, Fueled was without doubt one of the best sequels in a trilogy I’ve ever read. There’s no filler about it and the writing was brilliant. And yes, Driven was the appetizer to the main course of Fueled. With a tantalizing and much needed dessert to follow still in Crashed.<br><br>I was blown away to tears by the prologue and I just knew we had a great read ahead of us. Fueled had just about everything that keeps you addicted and excitedly reading. It had the passion between Rylee and Colton as well as some real emotional tear jerking moments.<br><br><b>“Why get attached to someone that will only leave in the end? To someone who will run the other way when they really know about the truths inside me. The poison that clings to my soul…” - Colton</b><br><br>The reveals were truly epic and the cliff hanger. Well…<br><br>Oh and sigh…Colton…<br><br><b>“Colton kisses like a man drawing his last breath and I am his air. It’s passionate and possessive and provocative.”<br><br>Jenny:</b> I was sobbing in the prologue. It really hit a nerve with me. It was extremely intense and a deeply moving introduction and set the scene for what was to be the unraveling of Colton Donavan. The man, the myth and just exactly what this 747 load of baggage he carried around consisted of and I have to say, the way the author handled this story was beautifully done. I can’t fault it.<br><br><b>“And it is in this moment, being witness to his agony, I realize there are so many different ways a person can ache. So many definitions I never realized behind a simple word. “</b><br><br>We got emotion in bucket loads and I fell in love with Colton even more if that’s at all possible, and I felt that Rylee really grew in Fueled, she became stronger and I can only see her coming into her own more and more as the trilogy concludes in Crashed.<br><br><b>“There’s so much that I need to explain to you. So much I need to say…so much I should have already said to you.”</b><br><br>Oh don’t get me wrong. There were times the miscommunication between these two drove me crazy and their unwillingness to bend frustrated me but both these characters have so many issues to deal with and learning to trust, love and depend on another is something they must commit to together and watching it unfold through the pages is gripping!<br><br><b>“This is what I do for a living and I missed all of the signs. Love and hurt overriding my training.”</b><br><br>And did I mention Colton…swoon…I love him! This troubled, broody, sensual man has stolen my heart.<br><br><b>“The image of Colton – so magnificent in body yet conflicted in mind and isolated in emotion…”<br><br>Gitte:</b> I fell even more in love with Colton if that was possible too. My heart aches for him, his childhood, the open wounds he still carries and I sympathise with him and understand his behaviour even more now.<br><br><b>“You at least deserve someone that’s going to try to be what you need…give you what you want…and I don’t think I’m capable of that.” - Colton</b><br><br>Really, for me this was Colton’s book, we got his story and how his past affects his here and now as well as his relationship with the gorgeous Rylee.<br><br>We really did get underneath that hard and controlling exterior which hides a damaged soul and a vulnerability that melts your heart.<br><br><b>“She pushes me. Unmans me. Consumes me. Scares the ever – loving shit out of me.” - Colton</b><br><br>As for Rylee, she really did do a lot of growing up. She needed to transfer her compassion and understanding from her profession into her personal life in order to understand and heal Colton. Not only that, she needed to realise a few important things about herself and her own past too. Overcome her insecurities and the tragedy which mars her life.<br><br><b>“I came back. For you. For me. For who we are when we’re together. For the possibilities of what we can be if you’ll just let me in…” – Rylee</b><br><br><b>Jenny:</b> Fueled really did exceed my expectations. I expected this to be a bit of a romp-fest to be honest but what we got was something so far removed from that scenario. We had questions answered, we witnessed Rylee and Colton grow and understand each other more. Getting into Colton’s head was a revelation. His internal thought processes humoured me and broke me.<br><br>This man has been through so much and you know that Rylee is just the woman to expel his demons and show him love beyond anything he imagined, if he will just let down those walls.<br><br><b>“Just listen to me Ry…If you really love him, then keep knocking on that fucking steel gate he has around his heart. If he’s worth it to you, you’ll keep at it.”<br>“The damn thing’s got to give sometime and you’re the only one I think is capable of doing it.”</b><br><br>I know a lot of readers are mentioning the CH word but I don’t consider the ending to be a cliff-hanger. OMG Yes! It killed me and I let out an audible “bloody hell” at the end but to me if felt like a perfect, heart racing ending and set the scene for Crashed. It had my adrenaline pumping, I was on the edge of my seat, I was cursing the author but…….isn’t that how I’m supposed to feel. This is a trilogy after all and I need to want that third book as much as I do my next breath, and I do. I’d say the author achieved that and more. The ending left me gasping and needing more! Roll on Crashed!!!<br><br><b>Gitte:</b> Fueled gave us a bit of everything we love. Passion, humour, angst and drama. It was so well written and whilst I got annoyed a few times at the misunderstandings and the behaviour it took nothing away from how brilliant a second instalment this is. I already miss Colton like crazy…I am irrevocably in love with this man!!! The cliff – hanger well….just see it as a momentary ‘pit stop’……<br><br><b>“I’ve never let someone this far in because that means secrets are shared and pasts are discovered. And because it means you need. I’ve only ever needed myself – needing others only results in pain. In abandonment. In unspeakable horror. And yet, I need Rylee right now.” – Colton</b><br><br><i>ARC Supplied by author in exchange for an honest review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13336333852252397287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Plamena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14813237-plamena"><img alt="Plamena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405071408p2/14813237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/877580967?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Plamena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Plamena" href="/user/show/14813237-plamena">Plamena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer877580967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15508893534061463786"><b>4.5 “I race Colton” stars</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <b>“She pushes me. Unmans me. Consumes me. Scares the ever-loving shit out of me.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Well…well…To say I was surprised would be a total understatement. I DID NOT expect to like this book so much but I did!!! It is so much better than the first one! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405400ra/789655.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Colton and Rylee’s ‘relationship’ is taking a different road. They both try to change and to be what the other person needs. But again…some might say they both are too fucked up to succeed. Granted, their pasts are just…there ar</span>
  <span id="freeText15508893534061463786" style="display:none"><b>4.5 “I race Colton” stars</b> <br><br><i>
  <b>“She pushes me. Unmans me. Consumes me. Scares the ever-loving shit out of me.”</b>
</i><br><br>Well…well…To say I was surprised would be a total understatement. I DID NOT expect to like this book so much but I did!!! It is so much better than the first one! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405400ra/789655.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Colton and Rylee’s ‘relationship’ is taking a different road. They both try to change and to be what the other person needs. But again…some might say they both are too fucked up to succeed. Granted, their pasts are just…there are no words. My heart was breaking for both of them. The cruelty that Colton has experienced as a child is just…too much. I have to admit this was quite hard to read.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I might not be able to tell you the things you need to hear with the traditional words you need to hear them in, but I swear to God, Rylee, I will try. And if I can’t, then I’ll show you. I’ll show you with everything I have—anything it takes—where your place is in my life”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408036ra/797783.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of the most important things about this book is that Colton got his identity. He is charming, fun, playful, dominating, really sweet, sometimes A TOTAL asshole but at least now I can easily differentiate him from Christian Grey and Gideon Cross. This was my biggest issue with the first book. Now when the problem is solved...I became Colton’s biggest fan!!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394699939ra/8892687.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There is a cliffhanger and THANK GOD the third book is out already!!!!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15508893534061463786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/870319278?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="-C-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="-C-" href="/user/show/29144518--c-">-C-</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer870319278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17654801855471414858"><i> Re-read september 2016 </i><br/><br/>Fueled picks up where my heart was shattered at the end of Driven. Colton and Rylee's relationship was and still is a roller coaster of passion, sexual chemistry and tension.<br/><b> <i> <blockquote> “I race you, Ryles.” </blockquote></i></b>  <br/>The banter between the two leads and even the secondary characters is funny at times and enjoyable to read. <br/> <b> <i> <blockquote> “We're not broken baby...we're just bent. And bent's okay. Bent means that we're just figuring things out.” </blockquote></i></b>  </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O9SjTQfb7/1spnjy+kmZTkDIdeWvHe3GW+cxlR5XjQV85QcrMCdLJZoiY8+S3TdZOo1sCTGvBn6Wnr/3/lLeFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jvO3q9HpdRGQfeRUUuyNWiSpEdWmDXuvZo4A47J5JRvJwhPN5hXRyWb5/2k6eCNNXuwIOTi/kBer946BUnx2Cw==')})
  }

THE HARSH REALITY After everything that’s happened, the rise and the fall, the pain and the aftermath, can these two navigate the waters of acute regret, survive the trials of coming face to face with all that they have lost, and find the strength to try again? <span id="freeTextContainer8929461082242382561"><b><i>New York Times</i> Bestselling author K. Bromberg writes contemporary novels that contain a mixture of sweet, emotional, a whole lot of sexy, and a little bit of real. She likes to write strong heroines, and damaged heroes who we love to hate but can’t help to love.<br/><br/>A mom of three, she plots her novels in between school runs and soccer practices, more often than not with her laptop in tow.<br/><br/>Since publish</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8929461082242382561" style="display:none"><b><i>New York Times</i> Bestselling author K. Bromberg writes contemporary novels that contain a mixture of sweet, emotional, a whole lot of sexy, and a little bit of real. She likes to write strong heroines, and damaged heroes who we love to hate but can’t help to love.<br /><br />A mom of three, she plots her novels in between school runs and soccer practices, more often than not with her laptop in tow.<br /><br />Since publishing her first book on a whim in 2013, Kristy has sold over one and a half million copies of her books across sixteen different countries and has landed on the New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal Bestsellers lists over thirty times. Her Driven trilogy (Driven, Fueled, and Crashed) is currently being adapted for film by Passionflix with the first movie, Driven, releasing August 10th.<br /><br />With her imagination always in overdrive, she is currently scheming, plotting, and swooning over her latest hero. You can find out more about him or chat with Kristy on any of her social media accounts. The easiest way to stay up to date on new releases and upcoming novels is to sign up for her newsletter (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/254MWtI">http://bit.ly/254MWtI</a>) or text KBromberg to 77948 to receive text alerts when a new book releases.<br /><br /><br /><br /></b><br /><br /><br /><b>Social Media Links:</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://facebook.com/AuthorKBromberg">https://facebook.com/AuthorKBromberg</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pinterest.com/KBrombergWrites/">http://pinterest.com/KBrombergWrites/</a><br />Instagram: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/kbromberg13/">https://instagram.com/kbromberg13/</a><br />twitter: @KBrombergDriven<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.KBromberg.com">www.KBromberg.com</a> <br /><br /><b>Completed Titles:</b><br />Series:<br /><i> The Driven Series</i><br />Driven<br />Fueled<br />Crashed<br />Raced<br />Aced<br /><br /><i>The Player Duet </i><br />The Player<br />The Catch<br /><br />Standalones<br />UnRaveled<br />Slow Burn<br />Sweet Ache<br />Hard Beat<br />Down Shift<br />Sweet Cheeks<br />Sweet Rivalry (1,001 Dark Nights Series)<br /><br />Everyday Heroes Standalones<br />Cuffed <br />Combust<br />Cockpit - Late Spring 2018</span>
